          <hr class="hrule"><br>
      
      
        <h3 id="sect1517"><span class="b_heading">Electrochemical characterization</span></h3>
        <span>Coin half-cells were assembled using P2-Na<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> or P2-Na<small><sub>0.60</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> as the cathode active material. The galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) was performed to evaluate the quasi-open circuit voltage (OCV) curve for both materials. The results of the GITT experiments are presented in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3</a>, where an OCV hull curve is added as a blue line and the on-load hull curve is presented in red colour.</span>
        <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig3"><a href="/image/article/2025/TA/d4ta04786a/d4ta04786a-f3_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d4ta04786a-f3.tif" src="/image/article/2025/TA/d4ta04786a/d4ta04786a-f3.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 3 </b> <span id="fig3"><span class="graphic_title">GITT measurements for (A) Na<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> and (B) Na<small><sub>0.60</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> as CAM. The OCV for various stoichiometries is highlighted as a blue hull curve, and the on-load hull curve is highlighted in red colour. For both materials, d<span class="italic">Q</span>/d<span class="italic">V</span> analysis of the OCV curve is included in the inset.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
        <p class="otherpara">For P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> both the OCV and on-load voltage curves exhibit distinct voltage jumps at <span class="italic">x</span> ≈ 2/3, 1/2 and 1/3 (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3A</a>). These voltage jumps are accompanied by flat voltage regions as evidenced by the d<span class="italic">Q</span>/d<span class="italic">V</span> plot (inset of <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3A</a>). In the literature, these voltage jumps are associated with distinct Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy orderings.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit44"><sup><span class="sup_ref">44,46</span></sup></a> The flat voltage profiles in proximity to these voltage jumps correspond to order/disorder transitions between unordered and Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy ordered phases.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit48"><sup><span class="sup_ref">48,83,88–92</span></sup></a> The voltage profile of P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>, – both at equilibrium and under current load – is considerably smoother than those of P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3A and B</a>). At the same sodium stoichiometries <span class="italic">x</span> = 2/3, 1/2 and 1/3, the voltage profile exhibits small shoulders in accordance with smaller peaks in the d<span class="italic">Q</span>/d<span class="italic">V</span> analysis (inset of <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3B</a>).</p>
        <p class="otherpara">Whereas the nature of the actual Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy orderings have been reported in the literature for P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>, to the best of our knowledge, for P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>, the nature of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy orderings has not been elucidated so far. However, the similarities in composition and structure suggest similar Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy orderings in both materials. The significantly reduced voltage jumps for P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> compared to P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> hint to partially suppressed or disrupted Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy orderings in P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>.</p>
        <p class="otherpara">To further investigate the nature and extent of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy orderings in both materials, synchrotron <span class="italic">operando</span> XRD measurements were performed. Waterfall diagrams of the obtained diffraction patterns are presented in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig4">Fig. 4A and B</a> for P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> and P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>, respectively. For both materials, the measurements start with sodiation from the charged state. The diffraction patterns corresponding to sodium contents of <span class="italic">x</span> = 2/3, 1/2 and 1/3 are highlighted in red, magenta and green colour, respectively. For P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>, clear superstructure reflections in proximity to the sodium content of <span class="italic">x</span> = 2/3, 1/2 and 1/3 are apparent. Simulated diffraction patterns based on the reported in-plane Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy ordering by Lee <span class="italic">et al.</span><a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit46"><sup><span class="sup_ref">46</span></sup></a> and Huang <span class="italic">et al.</span><a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit83"><sup><span class="sup_ref">83</span></sup></a> are presented in ESI Fig. S11,<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a> in which the range of experimentally found superstructure reflections is highlighted in yellow colour for the ease of comparison. At sodium stoichiometries of <span class="italic">x</span> = 2/3 and 1/3, the observed superstructure reflexions match the simulated pattern based on the Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy ordering reported by Lee <span class="italic">et al.</span><a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit46"><sup><span class="sup_ref">46</span></sup></a> For <span class="italic">x</span> = 1/2, observed superstructure reflections match the report by Huang <span class="italic">et al.</span><a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit83"><sup><span class="sup_ref">83</span></sup></a> in accordance with a previous publication.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit65"><sup><span class="sup_ref">65</span></sup></a></p>
        <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig4"><a href="/image/article/2025/TA/d4ta04786a/d4ta04786a-f4_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d4ta04786a-f4.tif" src="/image/article/2025/TA/d4ta04786a/d4ta04786a-f4.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 4 </b> <span id="fig4"><span class="graphic_title">Synchrotron <span class="italic">operando</span> XRD for (A) Na<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> and (B) Na<small><sub>0.60</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>. Both measurements were started in a charged state. The diffraction patterns corresponding to sodium stoichiometries of <span class="italic">x</span> = 1/3, 1/2 and 2/3 are highlighted in red, magenta and green colour, respectively.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
        <p class="otherpara">For P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>, similar superstructure reflections in proximity to <span class="italic">x</span> = 2/3 and 1/3 are apparent, however, the superstructure reflection at <span class="italic">x</span> = 2/3 is very weak. For P2-Na<small><sub>1/2±<span class="italic">δ</span></sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>, no superstructure reflection is observed, indicating that no long-range Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy ordering exists at this stoichiometry. The comparably low intensity of the Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy superstructure reflection in P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> is indicative of either decreased long-range order (disrupted ordering) or a smaller weight fraction of the ordered phase (partial ordering). For both materials, the similarity of the superstructure reflection at <span class="italic">x</span> = 2/3 and 1/3 supports the assumption that the in-plane Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy ordering is the same for both materials. These observations are in accordance with diffraction patterns obtained by <span class="italic">ex situ</span> capillary transmission XRD, as presented in ESI Fig. S12.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a> For both materials, the heat maps of the obtained diffraction patterns as well as the refined lattice parameters (Pawley method) are presented in ESI Fig. S13 and S14.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a> A good agreement of refined lattice parameters as well as the nature and extent of the detected Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy ordering is found for synchrotron <span class="italic">operando</span> XRD and <span class="italic">ex situ</span> capillary transmission XRD, indicating that the <span class="italic">operando</span> measurement is close to equilibrium.</p>
        <p class="otherpara">To measure the extent of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy orderings at various stoichiometries, entropymetry measurements were performed. A detailed description of the method is provided in the ESI.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a> In short, the equilibrium voltage at different sodium contents was measured at 40 °C, 25 °C and 10 °C following a GITT procedure including temperature change at every equilibrium step. The change in measured equilibrium voltage <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>OCV</sub></small> with the change in temperature Δ<span class="italic">T</span> is proportional to the entropy change Δ<span class="italic">S</span> at the corresponding sodium content <span class="italic">x</span>, according to:<br></p><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgugt4"><a href="/image/article/2025/TA/d4ta04786a/d4ta04786a-t4_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d4ta04786a-t4.tif" src="/image/article/2025/TA/d4ta04786a/d4ta04786a-t4.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td><a id="ugt4"><span id="ugt4"></span></a></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div><p></p>
        <p class="otherpara">Several factors, such as the configurational entropy, phonon entropy and electronic entropy, can contribute to the entropy change of a material.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit93"><sup><span class="sup_ref">93</span></sup></a> However, the course of the entropy change is reported to be highly dominated by the configurational entropy,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit93"><sup><span class="sup_ref">93</span></sup></a> making entropymetry a valuable tool to investigate it.</p>
        <p class="otherpara">The entropy change derived from several independent cells is presented in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig5">Fig. 5A and B</a> for P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> and P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>, respectively. For P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>, the entropy change curve exhibits a distinct double-S shape in proximity to sodium contents <span class="italic">x</span> ≈ 2/3, 1/2 and 1/3. As described in the ESI,<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a> such a double-S shaped course of the entropy change is expected in proximity to Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy ordered phases. For P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>, the entropy change curve follows a double-S shape at <span class="italic">x</span> ≈ 2/3, 0.54, 1/2 and 1/3, indicative of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy ordering at these stoichiometries. For P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>, the variation of entropy change at <span class="italic">x</span> ≈ 2/3 and 1/2 is significantly smaller compared to P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>, indicating a reduced extent of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy orderings in the former material. The double-S shaped course of the entropy change in proximity to <span class="italic">x</span> ≈ 0.54 might correspond to a weak Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy ordering resembling the reported Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy ordering in Na<small><sub>4/7</sub></small>CoO<small><sub>2</sub></small>.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit90"><sup><span class="sup_ref">90,92,94</span></sup></a> We have estimated the expected potential jump based on the measured configurational entropy change and summarized the estimated potential differences due to Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy orderings in ESI Table S8.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a> The results further corroborate more pronounced Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy orderings at <span class="italic">x</span> = 2/3 and 1/2 for P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> compared to P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>. Furthermore, the measured voltage jumps in GITT measurements (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3</a>) at <span class="italic">x</span> = 2/3, 1/3 in P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> and at <span class="italic">x</span> = 1/3 in P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> significantly exceed the estimated potential jumps due to configurational entropy change (<span class="italic">i.e.</span>, Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy ordering), suggesting additional processes contributing to these voltage jumps. For <span class="italic">x</span> = 2/3 in P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>, the energy difference between Ni<small><sup>2+/3+</sup></small> redox and Mn<small><sup>3+/4+</sup></small> redox is expected to significantly contribute to the voltage jump at <span class="italic">x</span> = 2/3 in P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>. For both materials, the onset of the P2–O2 phase transition is expected to contribute to the voltage jump at <span class="italic">x</span> = 1/3.</p>
        <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig5"><a href="/image/article/2025/TA/d4ta04786a/d4ta04786a-f5_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d4ta04786a-f5.tif" src="/image/article/2025/TA/d4ta04786a/d4ta04786a-f5.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 5 </b> <span id="fig5"><span class="graphic_title">Entropymetry measurements for (A) Na<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> and (B) Na<small><sub>0.60</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>. A detailed description of the method is provided in the ESI.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a> Jumps in the entropy change indicative of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy ordering are highlighted with coloured background. A GITT measurement is provided in grey colour in the background. For both materials, the results from independent cells are presented in different colour. The uncertainty of the linear regression is presented as error bars.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
        <p class="otherpara">Overall, GITT, <span class="italic">operando</span> XRD, <span class="italic">ex situ</span> XRD, and entropymetry indicate similar Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy orderings at <span class="italic">x</span> = 2/3 and 1/3 in P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> and P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>. For <span class="italic">x</span> = 2/3 and <span class="italic">x</span> = 1/2, XRD and entropymetry measurements suggest a disrupted Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy ordering in P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>. For <span class="italic">x</span> = 1/3, no significant influence of the Ni/Mn ratio on the Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy ordering is detected.</p>
        <p class="otherpara">In general, Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy orderings in these structures result from the high stability (low Gibbs free enthalpy) of the ordered configurations. In Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy ordered phases, Gibbs free enthalpy is eventually reduced by (i) minimized Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>–Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> repulsion within the sodium layer and (ii) advantageous interaction of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> with the immediate environment of the MO<small><sub>2</sub></small> slab (<span class="italic">i.e.</span>, low energy sodium lattice sites). For the herein investigated materials, the transition metals, nickel and manganese, are known to adopt different formal oxidation states depending on the applied electrode potential.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit50"><sup><span class="sup_ref">50,87</span></sup></a> Hence, the stability of sodium sites is eventually influenced by the transition metals in the immediate environment and the formal oxidation states thereof. The resulting difference in energy for various sodium sites potentially contributes to the preferential occupation of these sites (<span class="italic">i.e.</span>, preferential occupation of low-energy sodium sites).</p>
      
      
        <h3 id="sect1825"><span class="b_heading">Computational</span></h3>
        <span>Computational methods were employed to gain further insights into the origin of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy orderings in P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> and P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>. First, we identify the thermodynamically stable phases. Then, we evaluate the electronic structure and the charge density distribution of the transition metals in these materials. Subsequently, we evaluate the existence of low-energy sodium lattice sites in the absence of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>–Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> repulsion. Finally, we analyse the charge ordering within the MO<small><sub>2</sub></small> slab and correlate these findings with the existence and stability of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy orderings.</span>
        <p class="otherpara">Spin polarized periodic DFT calculations were performed to determine the thermodynamically stable phases and construct the convex hull for P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> and P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>. For P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>, the implemented unit cell includes 24 transition metal atoms arranged in a characteristic honeycomb Ni/Mn ordering in accordance with our characterization results and the literature<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit60"><sup><span class="sup_ref">60</span></sup></a> (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">Fig. 6A</a>). By substituting every fourth Ni by Mn, the unit cell for P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> with a defect honeycomb transition metal ordering is obtained according to the characterization results (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">Fig. 6B</a>). Even though the in-plane sodium arrangement has been reported for the Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy orderings at <span class="italic">x</span> = 2/3, 1/2 and 1/3 in P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit46"><sup><span class="sup_ref">46</span></sup></a> to the best of our knowledge, the relation of this in-plane sodium ordering to the honeycomb ordered MO<small><sub>2</sub></small> slabs has not been analysed so far. To fill this gap, we have calculated the free enthalpy for the reported in-plane sodium vacancy orderings at various sites in these large Ni/Mn ordered superstructure cells. The calculated convex hull is presented in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">Fig. 6C and D</a> for P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> and P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>, respectively. For P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>, solely the O2-structure at <span class="italic">x</span> = 0 and the Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy ordered P2-structures at <span class="italic">x</span> = 1/3, 1/2 and 2/3 are located on the convex hull. At <span class="italic">x</span> = 1/2, the Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy ordering, as reported by Huang <span class="italic">et al.</span>,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit83"><sup><span class="sup_ref">83</span></sup></a> was calculated to be energetically favourable, which is in accordance with our <span class="italic">operando</span> XRD results and literature reports for Na<small><sub>1/2</sub></small>CoO<small><sub>2</sub></small>.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit90"><sup><span class="sup_ref">90,91,95–99</span></sup></a> At <span class="italic">x</span> = 2/3, the determined stable structure exhibits the same in-plane Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy ordering;<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit98"><sup><span class="sup_ref">98,99</span></sup></a> however, the stacking sequence differs from reports on P2-Na<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>CoO<small><sub>2</sub></small>.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit90"><sup><span class="sup_ref">90,100,101</span></sup></a> For P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>, the O2-structure at <span class="italic">x</span> = 0 and the P2-structures at <span class="italic">x</span> = 1/3, 5/12, 1/2, 7/12 and 2/3 are located on the convex hull. At <span class="italic">x</span> = 1/2, the reported ordering by Lee <span class="italic">et al.</span><a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit46"><sup><span class="sup_ref">46</span></sup></a> was calculated to be slightly more stable than the ordering reported by Huang <span class="italic">et al.</span><a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit83"><sup><span class="sup_ref">83</span></sup></a> The marginal difference in energy between both orderings is in accordance with the disrupted Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy ordering observed with <span class="italic">operando</span> XRD and entropymetry measurements.</p>
        <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig6"><a href="/image/article/2025/TA/d4ta04786a/d4ta04786a-f6_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d4ta04786a-f6.tif" src="/image/article/2025/TA/d4ta04786a/d4ta04786a-f6.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 6 </b> <span id="fig6"><span class="graphic_title">Honeycomb transition metal ordering in (A) P2-Na<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> and in (B) P2-Na<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> and the corresponding convex hull for the Na intercalation for (C) P2-Na<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> and (D) P2-Na<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>. The Ni atoms are coloured in grey, Mn atoms in magenta, and O atoms in red. The additional Mn atoms located on Ni sites in (B) are highlighted in green. In (A and B), the supercell employed in the DFT calculations is shown in black. In (C and D), the formation energy per formula unit for Na configurations in the P2 structures and the O<small><sub>2</sub></small> structures are shown in red and blue, respectively.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
        <p class="otherpara">In general, configurations located on the convex hull (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">Fig. 6C and D</a>) are stable, whereas all configurations with formation enthalpies above the convex hull are unstable or metastable. The convex hull directly relates to the enthalpy difference between sodium in intercalated and metallic form, whereas the measured OCV curve, as presented in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3</a>, represents the Gibb's free energy (enthalpic plus entropic contribution) of the same reaction. In the convex hull, segments of solely unstable configurations (<span class="italic">e.g.</span>, 0 &lt; <span class="italic">x</span> &lt; 1/3 in P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>) represent a miscibility gap between the respective stable endmembers (<span class="italic">e.g.</span>, O2-Na<small><sub>0</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> and P2-Na<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>). The corresponding two-phase reaction results in a characteristic voltage plateau in the electrochemical potential profile.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit102"><sup><span class="sup_ref">102</span></sup></a> Overall, the calculated convex hull well describes the course of the experimentally determined OCV curve, suggesting that the enthalpy change dominates the course of the Gibb's free energy, however, small differences between the convex hull and the experimentally derived OCV curve exist. For P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">Fig. 6C</a>), the miscibility gap in the ranges 1/3 &lt; <span class="italic">x</span> &lt; 1/2 and 1/2 &lt; <span class="italic">x</span> &lt; 2/3 is expected to cause a voltage plateau. Experimentally, we find two small voltage plateaus associated with the order/disorder transitions in proximity to the respective Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy orderings and observe distinct voltage jumps for Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/vacancy ordered phases. The difference between the expected potential profile based on the convex hull and the measured voltage profile eventually arises from (finite) temperature effects. For P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">Fig. 6D</a>), no miscibility gap is expected between 1/3 &lt; <span class="italic">x</span> &lt; 2/3 based on the convex hull in line with the much smoother electrochemical voltage profile in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3B</a>.</p>
        <p class="otherpara">To elucidate the nature of the M–O and Na–O bonds, Density Overlap Regions Indicators (DORI)<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit103"><sup><span class="sup_ref">103</span></sup></a> were determined for P2-Na<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> as presented in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig7">Fig. 7</a>. The DORI analysis was developed to distinguish covalent from noncovalent interactions, while differences between metallic and ionic bonding cannot be resolved. In this framework, covalent interactions are revealed by localized overlap indicators, while noncovalent interactions are characterized by fully smeared out overlap indicators. This analysis is not restricted to interactions in molecules as similar bonding characteristics exist in solids and DORI was already successfully applied to Mn-oxides.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit104"><sup><span class="sup_ref">104</span></sup></a></p>
        <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig7"><a href="/image/article/2025/TA/d4ta04786a/d4ta04786a-f7_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d4ta04786a-f7.tif" src="/image/article/2025/TA/d4ta04786a/d4ta04786a-f7.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 7 </b> <span id="fig7"><span class="graphic_title">The DORI of the Na–O bond, the Mn–O bond, and the Ni–O bond in P2-Na<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>. DORI values of 1 imply overlapping density regions and are shown in blue while DORI values of 0 are shown in red.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
        <p class="otherpara">Hence, the DORI analysis in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig7">Fig. 7</a> allows tracking qualitative differences in bonding character between the different bonds in the system. Qualitatively identical results were observed independent of Na content and the Ni/Mn ratio and are depicted in ESI Fig. S15.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a> While the Mn–O and Ni–O bonds are characterized by localized basins of DORI values close to 1, indicating increased covalent character, the Na–O bonds show entirely smeared out overlap indicators implying ionic bonding. The revealed covalent nature of the M–O bond is in good agreement with what has been found for many other comparable oxides<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit104"><sup><span class="sup_ref">104,105</span></sup></a> and corresponds to a distribution of the electron density along the M–O bond. Thus, only formal oxidation states, which do not necessarily agree with the true charge at the ion, can be assigned. This observation is in accordance with the calculated Bader charges, which indicate lower electron density at the transition metal ion than that suggested by the formal oxidation state (see <a title="Select to navigate to table" href="#tab3">Table 3</a>).</p>
        
<div class="table_caption"><b>Table 3</b> <span id="tab3">The average local magnetic moment <span class="italic">μ</span> and the Bader charge of Mn and Ni for the lowest energy structures in P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/3</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>2/3</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> and P2-Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Mn<small><sub>3/4</sub></small>Ni<small><sub>1/4</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> for the Na contents <span class="italic">x</span> = 1/3, 1/2 and 2/3. The local magnetic moments constitute averages over all Ni and Mn atoms with the same formal oxidation state (OS) and variations were found to be negligible. Local magnetic moments and Bader charges associated with different oxidation states are separated by semicolons. At <span class="italic">x</span> = 0 both materials adopt the O2-structure</span>
		</div>
